Summary 168:
Accreditation and market surveillance of products from non-EU countries and the CE marking (Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 652/2002)
Accreditation & market surveillance
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EC) No 608/2002 on the accreditation, market surveillance, controls of non-European Union (EU) products and the European conformity marking
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a system of accreditation* for the assessment of products by national conformity assessment bodies (NCBs).
It sets out the conditions for the recognition of NCBs by EU countries.
KEY POINTS
National NCBs are recognised by the European Commission as competent bodies for the purpose of carrying out conformity assessments in the EU.
The purpose of the regulation is to ensure that national NCBs carry out their tasks in accordance with the principles of mutual recognition.
NCBs are not for profit and must not engage in activities that are not intended to add any gain to the resources of the body’s owners or members.
In order to ensure the proper functioning of their accreditation system, EU countries must monitor their NCBs regularly and take appropriate corrective measures within a reasonable timeframe where necessary.
EU countries must ensure that the NCBs that have been accredited by the Commission are made available to the competent authorities of the EU countries in order to carry out market surveillance checks on the products they assess.
Where an NCB is recognised by an EU country, it must be made public and, where appropriate, accessible to the conformity assessment authorities.
National NCBs must also be made available in the form of grants to the body recognised under this regulation without a call for proposals, or by the award of contracts to that or to other bodies, depending on the nature of the activity to be financed and on the financial situation of the NCB.
FROM WHEN DOES THE DECISION APPLY?
Directive 2001/95/EC has applied since 1 January 2002.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to improve the safety of consumer products. These include:
the harmonisation of the laws of the Member States on the labelling of products;
the introduction of a common framework for the marketing of products.
For more information, see:
Consistent products (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* CE marking: a product is CE marked if it meets all the essential requirements of EU law.
* Manufacturer: any person or body that has manufactured a product and has a legal responsibility to market it in the European Union.

Summary 169:
Arrest warrant: extradition procedure between the EU and the 3 Nordic countries and Iceland, Norway, the Kingdom of Norway and the Republic of Iceland (Agreement on extradition pursuant to an arrest warrant)
Arbitration procedure: extradition between the 3 countries and the EU
SUMMARY OF:
Agreement between the European Union (EU) and its Member States and the countries of the Nordic countries (Norway, Iceland and the United Kingdom of Iceland) on the extradition procedure for the purpose of prosecution or execution of sentences between the three countries
Decision 2002/852/EC — conclusion of the Agreement on extradition for the purposes of prosecution and execution of sentence
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND OF THE DECISION?
The agreement establishes a system for the extradition of persons who have been arrested in one of the three Nordic countries: Denmark, Norway and Iceland.
The decision concludes the agreement on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
The extradition procedure is based on a mechanism of surrender:
the arrest warrant;
the surrender of a person to the country of the issuing country; and
the execution of the arrest warrant.
An arrest warrant may be issued by a country having made a declaration that nationals will not be surrendered or that surrender will be authorised only under certain specified conditions.
A country may refuse to execute the warrant if it considers that the offence is punishable by a custodial sentence or detention order in the country in which issued the warrant or if it does not allow prosecution for the same offences when committed outside its territory.
In addition to the list of grounds for non-execution of the warrant is the following:
double criminality: the offence was committed in whole or in part in the territory of the executing country or in a place treated as such as a place of special interest to that country;
there is a risk of double criminality, i.e. the same offence being committed by the same person in two different countries;
a description of the circumstances in which the offences were committed, including the time, place and degree of participation in the offence by the requested person;
any penalty imposed, if there is a final judgment, or the prescribed scale of penalties for the offence;
other consequences of the offence.
Norway and Iceland may make a declaration to the effect that, on the basis of reciprocity, the conditions set out hereafter shall not be applied under the terms of the agreement.
If the country issuing the warrant does not consider that a person will not surrender, it may decide to issue a warrant for the arrest of the person who has been arrested. The executing country may decide that the person in question does not have the right to be extradited.
There are also grounds for refusing to execute a warrant:
a person has not given his or her consent to be arrested;
an offence has been committed outside the country to which the warrant has been issued; or
the person is a national of a country other than that of the country which has issued it.
Where the country executing the warrant considers that it is not capable of carrying out the warrant, it can refuse to do so.
When a person is arrested, he or she must be informed of the reasons for the refusal and of the conditions under which they are to be surrendered. If they do not comply with these conditions, they may be returned to their country of origin.
Amendments to the agreement
The parties undertake to ensure that the extradition system between, on one hand, the EU, and the two countries on the other hand, consists of a system of surrender pursuant to a warrant issued by the country on whose territory the person is being arrested. This system will be based on the following mechanisms:
an alert system (SIS);
the extradition of the arrested person by means of the alert system;
reciprocity between the countries.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The Agreement entered into force on 1 July 2002.
BACKGROUND
   
 
The EU has adopted a number of measures to improve the extradition procedures between its member countries and its neighbouring countries. These measures include:
establishing a European Arrest Warrant Information System (EAWISA);
introducing a system to facilitate the exchange of information between the SIS and the judicial authorities of the countries which have issued the arrest warrants;
ensuring that the European Judicial Network (EJN) is set up.
For more information, see:
EU extradition procedures (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENTS
Council Decision 2002/884/EC of 27 June 2002 concerning the conclusion of an Agreement between the Council and the Member States of the Union and the Governments of the Three Countries, of the one part, and Norway, Iceland, the State of the Kingdom, the Union of the Free State of Iceland, Denmark and the State in question, concerning the surrender for prosecution or the execution of a sentence between the one party and the other party (



Summary 170:
Rail passengers’ rights — Regulation (EC) No 652/2006
Rail passengers' rights — Article 652(2)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 608/2006 on the rights of rail passengers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that rail passengers have a high level of consumer protection in the field of transport.
It lays down rules on:
the carriage of passengers by rail;
the information and service quality of rail services;
accessibility of trains for disabled persons and persons with reduced mobility;
facilities through which reservations may be made or tickets or through tickets may be issued to the extent that some or all of these facilities are made available to users.
KEY POINTS
Railways must ensure that:
passengers have the right to:
information on rail services and to travel by rail without undue difficulty;
to purchase tickets for rail journeys;
their personal security in railway stations and on trains and to manage risk.
Passengers must have access to the information and services provided by railway undertakings concerning:
fares and special conditions for rail services,
access to trains for persons with disabilities,
the accessibility of trains and the facilities on board.
Transport contract
A transport contract is a contract of carriage for reward or free of charge between a railway undertaking or a ticket vendor and the passenger for the provision of one or more transport services.
A ticket vendor may offer a ticket to a passenger for more than one transport service for the same transport contract.
The carriage of a passenger on a single transport contract must be accompanied by a statement of the conditions for the carriage of the ticket.
the ticket vendor must provide the passenger with information on the conditions of the carriage and of the train.
Railway undertakings must also provide information to passengers on the accessibility of railway services, access conditions of rolling stock, accessibility of passenger facilities and the facility on board, as well as on the management of risks to the personal security of passengers and the handling of complaints.
EU countries may grant temporary exemptions from the application of the regulation to long-distance domestic rail passenger services. These exemptions may be renewed, on a transparent and non-discriminatory basis, for a maximum period of 5 years.
In addition, EU countries may apply the rules of this regulation to urban, suburban and regional rail passenger journeys.
Exemptions from the regulation
The regulation does not apply to certain services or journeys because a significant part of the rail passenger service, including at least one scheduled station stop, is operated outside the EU.
Amendments to Regulation (Euratom).
Amending Regulation (EU) 2019/852 amends the regulation in line with the European Commission’s communication ‘Consumer Policy Strategy 2002-2006’, which sets out the objectives of the European Union in relation to rail passenger rights.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
Directive 2001/14/EC has applied since 1 January 2006.
Directives 2001/15/EC, 2001/16/EC and 2001/18/EC have applied since 31 December 2001.
BACKGROUND
The European Union has adopted a number of measures to improve the protection of passenger rights on the rail transport market. These include:
Article 153 of the Treaty on European Union on the right of the person to be treated fairly and with due regard to his or her health and safety;
Article 154 of the Lisbon Treaty on the approximation of the laws of the Member States to the principles of public administration and to the requirements of the Council of Europe on public procurement.
For more information, see:
Passenger rights on rail transport (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Passenger: any person travelling by rail.
* Railway undertaking: any public or private undertaking the activity of which is to provide transport of goods and/or passengers by railway on the basis that the undertaking must ensure traction.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Commission Implementing Decision 2001/13/EC of 21 December 2001 laying down the rules on the carriage by rail of passengers.
Successive amendments to Directive 2001/12/EC are incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Commission communication of 22 May 2006 on the implementation of the consumer protection policy in the area of rail transport. The European Union is committed to ensuring that rail transport is a high-quality, safe and secure mode of transport for all passengers and that passengers are treated with respect to their rights and to their personal security.

Summary 171:

Quality of Europe-wide statistical information on education and learning (EEC-E)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 establishing a common framework for the systematic production of Community statistics in education and training
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It establishes a common European statistical information system for the production of European Union (EU) statistics in relation to education, training, lifelong learning.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries. It covers:
education and training;

labor market statistics.

children’s studies;
students’ studies.
Data collection

the number of students and graduates;
education expenditure;
income and living conditions;
graduates’ living conditions.

Implementation of the regulation
Eurostat:
is responsible for:
collecting and processing the data;
transmitting the data to Eurostat;
preparing and analysing the results;

ensuring that the data sources are suitably suited to the requirements of Eurostat and the legal context of existing data sources.

inform the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD) of the measures taken to improve the quality and reliability of EU statistics in this field;
conduct pilot studies to be completed on a voluntary basis by the EU countries;
assist Eurostat in the preparation of a report on the implementation of this regulation;
make recommendations to the Commission on the use of the information it has obtained.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
It has applied since 14 February 2008.
BACKGROUND

establish the set of final electricity consumption statistics (see below).

the number of respondents;

make modifications to the list of sources of data,
modify the national electricity statistics,
the transmission arrangements,
establishing and modifying the nuclear statistics
the set of energy consumption.

Summary 173:
Rights of passengers and persons with reduced mobility in the transport of goods and passengers in the European Union (EU) — rules for non-discrimination and assistance during their journey (Regulation (EC) No 596/2006)
Rights and non-discriminatory contract conditions for passengers and passengers with reduced Mobility
RIGHTS OF PASSENGERS AND PASSENGER*
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation No 598/2006 — rules on the rights of passengers, passengers, disabled persons and persons of reduced mobility when travelling by bus and coach
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes rules for the rights and assistance of passengers travelling by public transport in the EU.
It aims to ensure that passengers have the same level of protection as those of other EU citizens.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
bus and coach passengers;
passengers and passengers’ representatives;
travel agents and terminal managing bodies.
Passengers must be fully informed of their rights under this regulation, so that they can effectively exercise those rights.
They must be provided with information regarding the service before and during the journey, including:
the timetable;
the conditions and conditions of the ticketing and ticketing procedures;
information on the conditions of access to the terminal;
access to the service;
conditions for the carriage of passengers in case of an accident arising out of the use of the bus or coach.
the right to a safe and proportionate assistance following the accident.
In addition, passengers are entitled to compensation for death, including reasonable funeral expenses, or personal injury, or loss of or damage to luggage due to accidents arising from the use.
The rules also apply to the following:
medical treatment and treatment of passengers following an accident;
refusal of refusal to carry the disabled person or to refuse to carry a disabled person.
Transport contract conditions
The contract conditions and tariffs applied by carriers must be offered to the general public without any direct or indirect discrimination based on the nationality of the final customer or on the place of establishment of the carriers, or ticket vendors within the Union.
Ticket prices
The ticket prices must not be less than:
EUR 220 000 per passenger;
€ 1 200 per item of luggage;
Eur 1 200 for each item of baggage;
e.g. less than € 220 000 for a round-trip ticket;
less than € 1,200 for a return ticket.
Non-discrimination
Carriers must:
not discriminate on the grounds of nationality;
not charge a higher fare than the average fare for the same journey;
ensure that all passengers are treated equally in terms of their mobility;
take all necessary measures to ensure the safety and security of the passengers and their luggage, in particular by:
ensuring that passengers are accompanied by a qualified person with a disability;
providing them with information and assistance in the event of accidents;
assisting them in the case of delays or cancellations of a regular service.
Disabled persons
Passenger representatives and terminal managers must ensure that:
all passengers are provided with adequate information on the services offered to them;
they have access to all available transport facilities;
there is no discrimination on grounds of their disability or their reduced mobility.
Terminal managing bodies must take into account the needs of disabled persons when designing and implementing new terminals, and as part of major refurbishments, in accordance with ‘design for all’ requirements.
Consultation and cooperation with stakeholders, professional associations and associations of customers, passengers and disabled persons
The European Commission must cooperate in order to adopt arrangements at national or European level for the implementation of this regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2006.
BACKGROUND
 
  ICT (European Transport Agency).
For more information, see:
‘Passenger rights’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Е 
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 550/2006 of 21 December 2006 on the rules on passenger rights and the conditions for non discrimination and assistance on the journey of persons and mobility in transport (OJ L 157, 24.12.2006, pp. 1–20)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EEC) no 550/06 have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

  i.e. Directive 2002/36/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 22 December 2002 on the harmonisation of the laws of the Member States relating to the carriage, taxation and administration of passengers by means of public transport and repealing Council Directives 90/314/EEC and 90/316/EC and Directives 93/8/EC, 93/9/EC.

Summary 174:
Statistics on aquaculture
Statistics on aquatic organisms
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 852/2008 on the production of Community statistics on the Aquaculture sector
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
 
It establishes a common legal framework for the systematic production of EU statistics for the EU’s fisheries sector.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation covers:
the annual production (volume and unit value) and the number of species of aquatic organisms (aquaculture, ornamental and plant species);
the production of hatcheries and nurseries in number of those species;
the number of molluscs and crustaceans in the wild and transferred to a controlled environment.
It does not cover:
transferred to a non-controlled environment;
aquariums;
tanks and raceways;
artificial units constructed above or below ground level capable of high rates of water interchange or with a high water turnover rate and highly controlled environment but without water recirculation.
EU countries must submit the data referred to in Annexes II, III and IV to the European Commission (Eurostat) within 12 months of the end of the reference calendar year. The period laid down in Article 4(3) of Decision 1999/468/EC shall be set at three months.
The Commission must submit an evaluation report every 3 years on the statistics compiled pursuant to this regulation.
Evaluation report
By 31 December 2011 and every three years thereafter, Eurostat must submit a report to the EU Parliament and the Council on the quality of the statistics it has compiled. The report must describe how the data were collected and compiled.

Summary 175:
Control and enforcement of fishing vessels in the North-East Atlantic fisheries
Control and Enforcement of Fishing Vessels
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1224/2009 on the application by the European Union of the scheme of control and enforcement applicable to fishing vessels operating in the waters of the Convention Area which lie beyond the waters under the fisheries jurisdiction of the contracting parties
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes the general rules and conditions for applying by the EU of the Scheme adopted by NEAFC.
The convention on future multilateral cooperation in North-east Atlantic fisheries, as amended by the Convention on the implementation of the Agreement on the conservation and management of fishery resources in the area defined by the convention, sets out the rules for the implementation by EU countries of the regulation.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all fishing vessels flying the flag of contracting parties and operating in EU waters.
EU countries must send to the European Commission, in a computer-readable form, a list of all vessels flying their flag and registered in the EU which are authorised to fish in the regulatory area, in particular the vessels authorised directly to fish for one or more regulated resources, and any amendments to the list. The list must include:
the number of fishing days since the start of fishing, or since the last catch report;
the estimated cumulative catches retained on board;
a daily report on the amount of fish discarded and the fishing depth and the number of fish on board.
Vessels must inform the Commission of the date and time, according to Universal Coordinated Time (UTC) of the transmission of a report and the radio call sign of the fishing vessel from which the catch has been off-loaded.
National authorities must notify the Commission within 15 days of the end of each fishing day of the 15th day of each month of the calendar year of the period covered by the regulation, in accordance with the rules laid down in Article 33 of Regulation (EC) No 624/2004 on the management of fisheries (see summary).
The Commission must adopt delegated acts in respect of detailed rules concerning lists of the fisheries to be notified, procedures for prior notification of entry into port and for the cancellation thereof as well as authorisation to land or transhipment.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
 
   
It has applied since 1 July 2009.
BACKGROUND
  The convention on the operation of fisheries in the north-eastern Atlantic (known as the ‘Convention Area’) was adopted in 2006.
For more information, see:
Fisheries: North East Atlantic Fisheries Convention (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Fishing vessel: any fishing vessel not flagged in a contracting party, including vessels for which there are reasonable grounds for suspecting them to be without nationality.
* Convention Area: an area defined in the Convention of the International Maritime Organization (IMO).
* Non-contracting party vessel: a vessel not flagging in an EU country.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  i.
Council Regulation (EU, Euratom, Member States of the one part, and the European Economic Area, meeting within the Council of the Union, of 3 July 2009 on the general application of the Regulation adopted by the Committee of the Regions of the European Parliament and of the Council on the Implementation of the Regulations of the Parties to the Convention (OJ L 347, 29.7.2009, pp. 1-11)
Successive amendments to Regulation (Euratom, Euratox, No 1212/2009 have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 176:
Ecolabel scheme: rules for the establishment and application of the voluntary EU Ecolabel Scheme
Ecolabelling scheme: details
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 652/2009 — rules for establishing and applying the voluntary European Union (EU) ecolabel system
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes the European Union’s (EU)* voluntary ecolabilisation scheme.
It aims to improve the environmental performance of products and to encourage higher environmental performance in all sectors for which environmental impact is a factor in consumer choice.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all food and feed products, except for medicinal products for human use, as defined in Directive 2001/83/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 6 November 2001 on the Community code relating to medicinal products, or for veterinary use, and to any type of medical device. It does not apply to products certified as organic.
Rules for the setting up and applying of the scheme
Each EU country must designate the body or bodies responsible for carrying out the tasks provided for in this regulation (‘the competent bodies’) and ensure that they are operational.
The competent bodies must ensure that the verification process is carried out in a consistent, neutral and reliable manner by a party independent from the operator being verified, based on international, European or national standards and procedures concerning bodies operating product-certification schemes.
They must also ensure that competent bodies meet the requirements laid down in Annex V.
Eligible products
the regulation sets out the criteria for the award of the EU EColabel and the conditions for the use of the EColombolabel.
A maximum number of products may be eligible for the Ecolabelled. The regulation does not cover:
food and feed;
energy-related products;
animal feed; and
animal health products.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 1 July 2009.
BACKGROUND
   
The European Commission has adopted a regulation on the setting of ecodesign requirements for energy related products in the EU.
For more information, see:
‘Ecolabsorbents’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 177:
Supplementary protection certificate for medicinal products
Supplementary Protection certificate
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1906/2006 — supplementary protection certificate
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It codifies and repeals Council Regulation (Euratom) No 1901/2006 on the provision of supplementary protection certificates for the marketing of medicinal products.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
any medicinal product protected by a valid basic patent and for which the first authorisation to place it on the market as a medicinal product was granted before the patent is granted, provided that the application for a certificate was lodged within 6 months of the date on which the patent was granted;
any product covered by a patent granted before 1 January 2000.
The protection conferred by a certificate may extend only to the products covered by the authorisation or authorisations to place them on the EU market.
It does not apply to products protected by national or European patents.
Expiry of the certificate
The certificate may lapse:
at the end of the period provided for in Article 13;
if the certificate holder surrenders it;
in the event that the annual fee laid down in Article 12 is not paid in time;
as long as the product no longer meets the conditions of protection.
Applying for an extension of the duration of a certificate
Where an application for an extended duration is pending, an application must include the particulars referred to in Article 7(3) of the regulation (see summary) and a reference to a certificate already filed.
Application for an application to extend the duration must include:
the number and date of authorisation granted and the product identified in that authorisation;
where relevant, the number of authorisations granted to place the product on the European market in accordance with Directive 2001/83/EC;
the duration of the extension.
If the application does not meet the conditions laid down, the applicant must ask the applicant to rectify the irregularity or settle the fee within a stated time. The applicant must also inform the competent authority of the EU country in which the application was lodged. The authority must inform the applicant of the reasons for its decision.
When the certificate lapses, notification must be published in the Official Journal of the European Union (Official Journal).
Appeals
The decisions of the competent authorities of EU countries are open to the same appeals as those taken in national law against similar decisions taken in respect of national patents. These decisions are binding on the holder of the patent.

Summary 178:
Convention on the jurisdiction of courts and tribunals in civil and commercial matters (OJ L 347, 30.11.1973)
Convention of the Hague on jurisdiction of the courts and courts of the countries bound by the Convention on the application of the laws of the European Community (Oj L 347)
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU) 2017/852 on the conclusion of the Convention of Amsterdam on the exclusive jurisdiction of European courts and the courts of European Union countries on matters relating to tort, delict or quasi-delict
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE CONVENTION AND OF THE DECISION?
The convention aims to ensure that the European Court of Justice (ECJ) has exclusive jurisdiction in all matters of law in the European Union (EU). It does not apply to revenue, customs or administrative matters.
The decision concludes the convention on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
Objectives of the convention
The Convention applies to:
any person who is domiciled in an EU country bound by this convention, irrespective of their nationality;
any party to a contract entered into by the consumer and the other party to the contract, both of whom are at the time of conclusion resident in the same EU country, and which confers jurisdiction on the courts in that country;
all persons who are liable for liability arising from the use or operation of ships, installations or aircraft, in particular loss of freight or charter-hire.
any one of the parties may be sued in the courts for the place where the harmful event occurred or may occur.
Any person who pursues commercial or professional activities in the EU country of domicile or directs such activities to that country or to several countries including that country and the contract falls within the scope of such activities.
Claims for limitation of liability
The court of the country in which the action is brought may also have jurisdiction over claims for limitation.
Where the law governing such direct actions provides that the policyholder or the insured may be joined as a party to an action, the same court may have jurisdiction.
Jurisdiction of courts
The courts of each EU country must have exclusive jurisdiction, regardless of the nationality of the defendant, in proceedings relating to the registration or validity of any European patent granted for that country irrespective of whether the parties are nationals of that country. The same court also has jurisdiction in proceedings which have as their object the validity of entries in public registers, and in proceedings where the register is kept in the country where the registration is kept.
A consumer may bring proceedings against a contract either in the court of that party or in the one for which the contract is entered into.
An employer may be brought against a consumer, except insofar as the insurance is compulsory or relates to immovable property in a State bound by that convention.
Insurers may also be sued, except in the case where the contract relates to the insurance of the insured.
In addition, the court in which an insurance policyholder is insured may bring a lawsuit against the insurer.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The agreement on jurisdiction entered into between the EU and the EU countries on the convention entered into force on 30 November 2017.
BACKGROUND
The Amsterdam Convention is one of a series of international conventions on jurisdiction which have been concluded by the European Economic Community (now the EU). The convention applies to all EU countries, except Denmark.
For more information, see:
‘The Hague Convention’ on the European Commission's website.
MAIN DOCUMENTS
Council Decision 2001/853/EC of 30 November 2001 on the entry into force of the Conventions of Amsterdam and of the Courts of the Governments of the Member States of the Union on the exercise of their exclusive jurisdiction over matters concerning the application, in civil matters, of the rules of jurisdiction there in force, and those specified in Annex I to the convention, and repealing Council Regulation (EEC) No 552/96 (O J L 347 of 30.10.2001)
Council decision (EU, Euratom) 2017 / 852 of 29 November 2017 on the approval of the Protocol of Amsterdam concerning the accession of the Council to the Convention in the field of jurisdiction conferred on it by the Council of the United Nations on the protection of persons and property against the effects of natural disasters and on the liability of persons, companies, undertakings and undertakings in the event of the occurrence of a natural disaster or of a harmful event.
